25:T2d2b,<entryFree id="n27791" key="عَبْدٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عَبْدٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, originally an epithet, but used as a subst., (Sb, TA,) <hi rend="ital">A male slave;</hi> (S, A, O, L, Msb, K;) <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَمْلُوكٌ</foreign>; (L, K;) [but <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدٌ</foreign> is now generally applied to <hi rend="ital">a male black slave;</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">مَمْلُوكٌ</foreign>, to <hi rend="ital">a male white slave;</hi> and this distinction has long obtained;] <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حُرٌّ</foreign>; (S, A, O, L, Msb;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-1" target="عَبْدَلٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27803"/></foreign>, (L, K,) in which the <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> is augmentative: (L:) and <hi rend="ital">a servant,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">worshipper,</hi> of God, and of a false god, or of the Devil: (Lth, L, &amp;c.:) [you say <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدُ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدُ الشَّمْسِ</foreign> &amp;c.: see also <foreign lang="ar">عَابِدٌ</foreign>, which signifies the same; and see the remarks in this paragraph on the pls. <foreign lang="ar">عَبِيدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عِبَادٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَبَدَةٌ</foreign> &amp;c.:] and <hi rend="ital">a man,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">human being;</hi> (M, A, L, K;) as being <hi rend="ital">a bondman</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">مَرْبُوبٌ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">to his Creator;</hi> (L;) applied to <hi rend="ital">a male</hi> and to <hi rend="ital">a female;</hi> (Ibn-Hazm, TA;) <hi rend="ital">whether free or a slave:</hi> (K:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَعْبُدٌ</foreign> (S, O, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">أَعْبِدَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَعْبَادٌ</foreign>, (IKtt, TA,) [all pls. of pauc.,] of which the first is the most commonly known, (Msb,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-2" target="عَبِيدٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27805"/></foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عِبَادٌ</foreign>, (S, O, Msb, K,) which two and the first are the most commonly known of all the many pls. of <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) <foreign lang="ar">عَبِيدٌ</foreign> being like <foreign lang="ar">كَلِيبٌ</foreign> as pl. of <foreign lang="ar">كَلْبٌ</foreign>, a rare form of pl.; (S, O;) or, accord. to some, it is a quasipl. n.; accord. to Ibn-Málik, <foreign lang="ar">فَعِيلٌ</foreign> occurs as a pl. measure, but sometimes they use it in the manner of a pl. and make it fem., as in the instance of <foreign lang="ar">عَبِيدٌ</foreign>, and sometimes they use it in the manner of quasi-pl. ns. and make it masc., as in the instances of <foreign lang="ar">حَجِيجٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَلِيبٌ</foreign>; (MF;) [accord. to the general and more approved opinion, it is a quasi-pl. n., and therefore fem. and masc., but most commonly fem.;] and further it should be remarked that the common people agree in making a difference between <foreign lang="ar">عَبِيدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عِبَادٌ</foreign>, by the former meaning <hi rend="ital">slaves</hi> [and by the latter meaning <hi rend="ital">servants</hi> of God and also simply, with the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">mankind</hi>], saying, <foreign lang="ar">هٰؤُلَآءِ عَبِيدٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">these are slaves,</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا عَبْدٌ مِنْ عِبَادِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">this is a servant, of the servants of God</hi>]: (Az, L:) [and a distinction is also made between <foreign lang="ar">عِبَادٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَبَدَةٌ</foreign>, respecting which see what follows:] other pls. of <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدٌ</foreign> are <foreign lang="ar">عُبْدَانٌ</foreign>, (S, O, K,) like <foreign lang="ar">تُمْرَانٌ</foreign> pl. of <foreign lang="ar">تَمْرٌ</foreign>, (S, O,) and <foreign lang="ar">عِبْدَانٌ</foreign>, (S, O, K,) like <foreign lang="ar">جِحْشَانٌ</foreign> pl. of <foreign lang="ar">جَحْشٌ</foreign>, (S, O,) and <foreign lang="ar">عُبُدٌ</foreign>, (S, O, K,) like <foreign lang="ar">سُقُفٌ</foreign> pl. of <foreign lang="ar">سَقْفٌ</foreign>, (S, O,) or this is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">عَبِيدٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">رُغُفٌ</foreign> pl. of <foreign lang="ar">رَغِيفٌ</foreign>, (Zj,) and is also a pl. of <foreign lang="ar">عَابِدٌ</foreign>, (L,) and some read [in the Kur v. 65] <foreign lang="ar">عُبُدَ الطَّاغُوتِ</foreign>, (Akh, S, O,) and <foreign lang="ar">عُبْدٌ</foreign> (MF) and <foreign lang="ar">عُبُودٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عُبَّدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عُبَّادٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَبَدَةٌ</foreign>, (IKtt, TA,) the last three of which are also pls. of <foreign lang="ar">عَابِدٌ</foreign>: (L:) one says of the worshippers of a plurality of gods, <foreign lang="ar">هُمْ عَبَدَةُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الطَّاغُوتِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">they are the servants of Et-Tághoot</hi>]; but the Muslims one calls <foreign lang="ar">عِبَادُ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">the servants,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">worshippers, of God:</hi> (Lth, L:) [all these are pls. in the proper sense of the term, of the broken class:] and <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدُونَ</foreign>, (O, K,) a pl. of the sound class, adopted because <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدٌ</foreign> is originally an epithet: (TA:) and [the following, with the exception of the first, and of some which are particularized as being pls. of pls., are also said to be pls., but are properly speaking quasi-pl. ns., namely,]   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-3" target="عَبُدٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27793"/></foreign>, (O, K,) accord. to some, who read [in the Kur ubi suprà] <foreign lang="ar">عَبُدَ الطَّاغُوتِ</foreign>, making the former a prefixed noun, as meaning <hi rend="ital">the servants</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">خَدَم</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">of Et-Tághoot;</hi> but it is a n. of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعُلٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">حَذُرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">نَدُسٌ</foreign>, not a pl.; the meaning being <hi rend="ital">the servant</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">خَادِم</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">of Et- Tághoot;</hi> (Akh, S, O;) and it is also used by poetic license for <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدٌ</foreign>; (Fr, T, S, O;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-4" target="عِبِدَّانٌ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-5" target="عِبِدَّآءُ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-6" target="عِبِدَّى" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27800"/></foreign>; (S, O, K;) or, accord. to some, the last of these signifies <hi rend="ital">slaves born in a state of slavery;</hi> and the <hi rend="ital">female</hi> is termed   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-7" target="عَبْدَةٌ" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27795"/></foreign>; and Lth says that   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-8" target="عِبِدَّى" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27800"/></foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">a number of slaves born in a state of slavery, generation after generation;</hi> but Az says that this is a mistake, that <foreign lang="ar">عِبِدَّى ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">عبَادُ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, that it is thus used in a trad., and that <foreign lang="ar">عِبِدَّى</foreign> is applied in another trad. to poor men of the class called <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلُ الصُّفَّة</foreign>; (L;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-9" target="عُبُدَّآءُ" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27791-10" target="عِبِدَّةٌ" n="10" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27799"/></foreign> and
